actions, which are primary and secondary search. In this case, the
primary search will be done. The illustration of the searching area
can be seen in 4.41. The primary search will require Firefighter
1 (F1) to walk with a thermal camera in the smoke area of the
fire compartment, while Firefighter 2 (F2) will help to protect the
F1 with a hose with water if needed. The secondary search is not
needed, the reason for that is that the sprinkler system and open
area will reduce the density of smoke, and the density of people on
the top floor of a parking building will be low

Figure 4.43: Hose establishment in fire compartment
The control of the fire is already done by SHT#1. The electrical
vehicle contains a lot of components that can burn beside the
battery as well, so the time that the car can burn will vary on a
lot of factors, this leads to a variation of the extinguishing process
from up to 120 minutes and in some cases more than that (if the
extinguishment tactic were chosen to be defensive). Everything
depends on the damage, size, type of battery, etc. Besides that,
the battery must cool down for 60 minutes before the car can be
hooked up to a trailer and transported away from the cellar. But
this can only happen if the required amount of water is satisfied,
which is 400 liters per minute, which relates to two C-type hose
attacks. Illustration of hose positioning in the fire compartment
can be seen in figure 4.43
94
Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:103==

Table 4.3 presented above describes a complete chronology of events, gathered during the
fire brigade’s intervention. It includes important timing details necessary for monitoring the
sequence of events. The table contains the time of registration of the fire, the fire brigade’s
arrival, the relay of orders, the start of the intervention, etc. Furthermore, times critical to
firefighters are highlighted in the table with a “(+ 20 min)” notation. This indicates that the
smoke helmet team (SHT) is expected to exit the compartment 20 minutes after deployment
in the compartment and wear the breathing apparatus. In addition, certain parts in this table
are interesting to discuss. Some of them are the travel and arrival times, the time to establish
a connection to a water supply, the time required for firefighters to conduct search and rescue
operations, and the process of controlling and extinguishing the fire.

4.1.4
Case 2 - Scenario 2
As in the previous scenario, the application of the fire brigade intervention model (FBIM) is
used in a case where the fire combustion happened in the parking building on the 6th floor. In
this scenario, only one brigade will arrive at the fire scene. The tactical approach of the fire
brigade is seen in the figure 4.46 below.
Usage of the charts follows a logical sequence, which is established based on Danish Fire
Intervention protocol and interview. This type of approach creates clarity and consistency in
the execution of tasks from registration of the fire to its extinguishment.
The process of gathering information and creating a tactic is based on the same methodology
as in scenario 1, the chart will be described at each step, to understand the process and what
data were used to create this tactic.
As in scenario 1 for the users’ purposes, orientation in the tactic will be done by providing
a sequential trajectory of chart usage on the left side of the page below and inserting a
representation of figure 4.46 in the top right corner, which will give an overview of where the
tacit user is positioned. The charts that are discussed on the current page will be indicated in
green color and the charts that the user already passed will be marked with grey color.

The combustion of the electrical vehicle (EV) started
in the parking building on the 6th floor, which led
to the spread of smoke towards the ceiling. The
temperature of smoke at the ceiling causes the acti-
vation of sprinkler systems in the fire compartment
above the EV (2 taps). Depressurizing the sprinkler
system causes the verification system to start. After
confirmation of the depressurizing of the system, the
system sends an alarm further to the fire service.
Model Input:
Time to activate automatic detection or
suppression system: sprinkler system 45.00 seconds

sprinkler system depressurizes in 50.00 seconds (> 2000m2)
[Table A (4), Figure 1]
Time delay for alarm verification: 20.00 seconds [Table B
(1)]
The time that is taken from the registration to send an alarm
further to fire services takes in a total of 115.00 seconds
The dispatch process of firefighters went through the sprinkler
detection system to the ABA system, which sends the message
straight to the dispatch system.
The system does everything
automatically, so there will be no delay in the form of receiving and
giving the information further. This is based on the computer-aided
dispatch system (CAD system) that is installed. Besides that, the
T˚arnby Fire Station (TMFS) receives messages simultaneously with
the alarm central.

Searching and rescue can begin after the water is charged in the
hose. The search and rescue are divided into two types of search
actions, which are primary and secondary search. In this case, the
primary search will be done. The illustration of the searching area
can be seen in 4.55. The primary search will require Firefighter 1
(F1) to walk with a thermal camera in the smoke area of the fire
compartment, while Firefighter 2 (F2) will help to protect the F1
with a hose with water if needed.
The secondary search is not needed, the reason for that is that
the sprinkler system, wind will reduce the density of smoke, and
the density of people on the top floor of a parking building will be
low.

Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design

The control of the fire is already done by SHT#1.
The electrical vehicle contains a lot of components
that can burn beside the battery as well, so the time
that the car can burn will vary on a lot of factors,
this leads to a variation of the extinguishing process
from up to 120 minutes and in some cases more
than that (if the extinguishment tactic were chosen
to be defensive). Everything depends on the damage,
size, type of battery, etc. Besides that, the battery

The table presented above describes a complete chronology of events, gathered
during the fire brigade’s intervention. It includes important timing details necessary
for monitoring the sequence of events. The table contains the time of registration
of the fire, the fire brigade’s arrival, the relay of orders, the start of the intervention,
etc. Furthermore, times critical to firefighters are highlighted in the table with
a “(+ 20 min)” notation. This indicates that the smoke helmet team (SHT) is
expected to exit the compartment 20 minutes after deployment in the compartment
and wear the breathing apparatus. In addition, certain parts in this table are interesting to
discuss. Some of them are the travel and arrival times, the time to establish a connection to a
water supply, the time required for firefighters to conduct search and rescue operations, and
the process of controlling and extinguishing the fire.

Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:123==
4.2
Results
The description provided above gives a great understanding of the method’s usage. It presents
a complete explanation and description of the steps, any user needs to undertake to perform
the FBIM simulations. However, before users can confidently say that the tactic is completed,
consultation with the authorities is required. Additionally, going through the detailed processes
involving the flowchart charts can present challenges, particularly when these charts include
sub-charts, and the tables lack the required option for the given situation. For those cases, an
illustrative example will be provided later in this chapter.
When a user designs a tactic using the flowcharts from the FBIM manual, the user automatically
integrates the Dataset. The charts and dataset create necessary steps within the tactic that
include the table or other forms of input. Typically, the table provides multiple action elements
to be adapted to current situations. As tactics vary, this may result in a scenario where the
table misses relevant data. However, the FBIM dataset provides data that covers the most
common firefighter procedures, including laying hoses, walking speeds, and charging hoses,
among others. In many cases, this dataset provides a reliable estimated procedure for the
accomplishment of specific tasks. But, in situations where the dataset does not have relevant
data, it can create challenges with time estimations of the tasks that firefighters have to carry
out. Furthermore, inconsistent use can lead to deviations from the realistic time estimation.
The estimations, used in this report are derived from the Danish authorities, Google Maps, and
various articles, which leads to a deviation from the ”original” application of the FBIM manual
and its dataset.
The tables provided data that are gathered in empirical measurements of firefighter performance.
The data gathered in the Australiasina dataset may differ from data that will be collected in
Denmark. The reason for these expected variations lies in tradition, tools, and tactics employed
in executing individual processes.
The usage of the table and its data occurs based on the specific information that is provided
by the case. For instance, Chart 8 in Case 1 Response 2 will be used, as this chart covers
numerous steps that require consideration and estimation. This example will be discussed in
the next section.
4.3
The Application of Tables and Data
Chart 8 combines two sub-charts,Chart 6 and Chart 9, alongside Tables M, O, Q, T, and
Tables G, F within Chart 8. When starting the usage of Chart 8, the user is met with the
question: ”Is road travel within the site necessary?”. This leads to the initial box, Box 3, titled
”Time for any security procedures,” which uses the Table G.
Figure 4.58: Table G
Given that security measures can vary
based on the design solution, the table
requires the user to specify both the kind
of security measure that is implemented
and the duration that is required to com-
plete this stage. Due to the large presence of security personnel at the airport, it is estimated
that it will take them approximately 4.5 seconds to open the roadblockers. This procedure
operates under two key assumptions: firstly, the security staff will be stationed near the control
center for the roadblockers, and secondly, they will have the capability to quickly open the gate
before or at the same time as the arrival of the fire engine at the security checkpoint.

all firefighters must be equipped with their BA gear, regardless of whether they are entering
the fire compartment or operating the pump close to the engine outside. This requirement
leads to a variation in the time from real-life scenarios because moving in BA gear reduces
speed and spends energy unnecessarily for firefighters who are not required to have that type
of equipment on.

4.4
Discussion
This section will primarily concentrate on analyzing and evaluating the various parts related
to the development of the tactic and software, including the use of manuals, datasets, and
feedback from authorities. Additionally, it will investigate the challenges faced in applying the
manuals and deviations from reality, as indicated by authorities.
Chart 1
The interview shows us that the ”Time to depressurize the system and activate the
alarm” amounts to 0 seconds, and similarly, the ”Time delay for alarm certification” is also
0 seconds. This information directly relates to the dataset. Table A offers details based on
the combined Occupants Hazard Information (OHI) and the Australian Standard (AS 2118.1).
However, the table does not allow for the use of a custom value, which was discovered during
the interview with authorities.
Chart 2
The involved Fire Stations receive information in different ways. When the ABA
system detects a fire, it automatically send out a signal to the alarm central and, simultaneously,
to the T˚arnby Municipality Fire Station. A similar process is assumed for the Store Magleby
Fire Station. The transmission of the signal from the signal to the respective fire stations
happening entirely automatic. But, for the Airport Fire Station West, the procedure differs
slightly. The ABA system handles the registration and sends the alarm to the Alarm Central,
which then directs it to ARFF with a 15-second delay. This delay is to prevent disruptions to
the airport traffic control dispatch system.
Chart 3
The firefighters are required to take their gear on and depart from the fire station
within a specific frame which depends on the fire station working schedule. However, the
airport fire brigade operates under a different time constraint, which requires that they must
leave the station within 30 seconds.
Chart 4
”Travel time” estimates provided by Google Maps are conservative. But, these
estimations are based on adherence to traffic rules. The fire engines operate at higher speeds
and may bypass traffic regulations if needed. Moreover, firefighters from the Airport West Fire
Department (ARFF) will take the airport’s internal road and arrive at the fire scene through
“Kongeporten”. This traveling path is not investigated because of the lack of information on
how fast and what internal road system the fire engine will take.
Chart 5 + 6
At arrival, if the officer in charge observes smoke without signs of the fire itself,
then the officer must rush to the fire central. This approach will give a clearer understanding
of where the fire occurred. However, if the fire is visible from the outside, for example, flames
are observable from windows, the firefighters will establish a water connection and advance
directly to the fire’s location without first visiting the fire central point at first. However, it is
still important for an officer in charge to visit the fire central to gain a complete understanding
of the fire’s situation.
Furthermore, the officer in charge (technical leader) often arrives in a separate vehicle, allowing
to position the vehicle in a different place. This arrangement permits the officer’s vehicle to
potentially reach the fire central at a closer point, thereby reducing the time and distance
required to move from the vehicle to the fire central location.
118
Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:127==
As Chart 5 moves to sub chart Chart 6, the first action required by the chart is to don the
breathing apparatus (BA). In a cellar scenario, this approach is logical since an OIC cannot
be sure if the safe conditions will be exceeded. However, in parking buildings, where the fire
central is on the ground level and separated from the building, wearing the breathing apparatus
may only reduce the OIC’s speed, so there need of modification of Table M to permit the
dismounting process without donning the BA equipment.
For security purposes, both the parking building and the cellar are equipped with CCTV, which
provides details about the fires origin, occupancy, and location. This information could be
useful in Chart 5 by introducing a step that asks whether the building is equipped with CCTV,
thereby offering the OIC more precise information before reaching the scene. Integrating this
step would allow the commanding officer to brief the firefighters before their arrival to the fire
scene.
Relay and Receive orders.
Chart 5 focuses on locating the fire place. However, once the
location is determined, the chart lacks an additional step where the officer in charge orders
the firefighters to move in. Integrating this step is necessary, either as an intermediary step
between charts 5, 7, or 8 or by adding it as the final step within Chart 5 itself.
Chart 10
The chart provides the establishment of the water supply, but it’s not specific about
how and who is responsible for different tasks. As the engine has to be connected to the dry
pipe and hydrant, there is a need to Figure out which of those two tasks takes the longest
time. This information is critical, as the water supply is the key element for the intervention
and extinguishment process. Moreover, most of the time data provided by the AFAC Dataset,
is in the opinion of fire authorities a bit too long. That could be caused by different tactics
and standards of establishment of water supply.
Chart 12
The search and rescue operations set a priority on the safety of the personnel
conducting these activities. However, there is no detailed description of the tools that need
to be used to accomplish the task. Danish firefighters, for instance, use thermal cameras for
search and rescue in smoke-filled rooms that might be occupied. This tool significantly reduces
the duration of both primary and secondary searches. Moreover, the range of areas aimed for
secondary search and rescue is significantly reduced because firefighters use thermal cameras to
determine the presence of any occupants within the fire compartment.
Chart 13 + 7
In the FBIM manual, the task of exposure protection is done by regular
firefighters. But the responsibility for managing this process has to fall on the officer in charge.
This is because the explanation of all aspects that the firefighter has to take into account
when executing the tasks can be overwhelming and misleading. Furthermore, after requesting
additional support, the officer in charge can undertake an exposure protection reconnaissance
himself. Doing so not only saves time but also helps in identifying the areas or properties that
need exposure protection. Based on this information, the tactic can be updated and executed.
However, conducting reconnaissance for exposure protection should be initiated by OIC and be
completed as outlined in chart 7.
Chart X1 and X2
As previously mentioned, the manual is created to handle most of the
tactics, but not all of them. In the cases that are used for this project, the charts did not
completely specify a method for deploying special vehicles after a request by the officer in
charge. This leads to a necessity of creation the necessity to devise new charts, Chart X1 and
X2. Chart X1 aims to guide the user on the route that the special vehicle and its crew should
Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
119
==PAGE:128==
take to reach a burning vehicle that is located within a parking lot. Similarly, Chart X2 aims to
explain the preparations required for the burning vehicle before transporting it outside of the
building. Besides that additional tasks may be given to the firefighter, such as managing the
fire during the vehicle transportation process.
Figure 4.65: Results from Software
Software:
Several major difficul-
ties appeared in the development of
the software. Among these problems
are those that are related to the lin-
earity and interface of the software.
The linear design forces users into a
situation where bypassing irrelevant
steps isn’t an option. This is clearly
the case for chart 6, specifically in
step 5. The design of a script that
is used strictly follows the selection
of options that are provided by the
manual and dataset or aborting the
entire script. The interface also cre-
ated challenges. At this stage, the
users have to be well-routed to use this software properly. It is hard for users to use software
confidently and keep an abstract position in the entire process. Currently, the user interface
consists simply of text outputs in the Python console, which can be seen in Figure4.65. Of
course, users can backtrack through the entire process to the beginning by scrolling in the
console, but this method can easily confuse the user. The software’s further improvement needs
to improve its user-friendliness.

==PAGE:129==
Chapter 5
Perspectivation
For individuals working with this material in the future, it is important to note that the creation
of models has brought up several factors, that must be considered, when using the information
from this thesis. The primary areas requiring further development and awareness include
updating tactics, creating new charts, improving software, and creating a dataset based on
Danish firefighter exercises. Each of these components will be discussed in the sections that
follow.
5.1
Tactical Development and Update
Establishing a tactic is important before the fire brigade can initiate the extinguishment process.
The methodology firefighters use to fulfill their duties is linear until the water connections are
established. But, once primary tasks are completed, the process can be unpredictable. This
sequence of actions leads to uncertain processes that move the tactic from practical realities,
thereby causing a deviation in timing and end tactic path.
5.2
Creation of additional paths and charts
The FBIM manual is created to simulate tactics but does not completely cover all aspects of
the scenarios. It became obvious after the investigation that some steps require additional
information. Consequently, this requires the user to create extra steps within the existing charts
and to formulate additional charts to describe the procedures for transporting and managing
the burning object.
The investigation showed a lack of charts dealing with transportation and preparation of
specialized vehicles. In addition, certain charts could integrate extra steps that will cover
additional important information, which will make the firefighters’ tasks easier and save time in
emergencies. Integrating these steps would make the tactic more “completed”, allowing it to
reach more unusual situations. As an example, the development of two supplementary charts,
Chart X1, and X2 could cover some of the unusual situations that appeared in this project.
Chart X1 describes the procedure for transporting the special vehicle to the fire scene. Chart X2
describes the process for moving a burning vehicle from either a parking garage or a residence.
Moreover, various boxes within the carts can be adjusted to be more flexible for the appearing
information. For instance, in Chart 6, Box 2, titled ”Time to dismount fire appliance and
don BA,” the procedure is connected to Table M. This step provides only a single option,
Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
121
==PAGE:130==
disregarding the fact that not every firefighter is required to use breathing apparatus (BA) after
dismounting from the engine.
5.3
Software update
The software has been developed based on the FBIM manual and is designed to be both simple
and functional. However, this software led to several issues that users are likely to face while
using it. A primary problem is the interface. Currently, it consists of a series of chosen steps
from the charts that are displayed in the Python console. The chosen steps become large and
difficult for users to keep track of. To handle this problem, there is a need for the development
of an interface that will show the whole process that the user has already gone through.
5.4
Danish version of FBIM Dataset
FBIM Dataset can be updated by including Danish numbers, in that way it will create more
accurate and time-realistic tactics. Data can be collected from firefighters’ yearly exercises and
compiled data into a dataset, allowing future manual users to develop tactics that are more
closely aligned with Danish reality.
122
Firefighter Engineering - Use of Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:131==
Chapter 6
Conclusion
In conclusion, the analysis of two cases, each with its own scenarios, shows that the application
of the FBIM manual in the context of the Danish emergency response is feasible. Denmark
has developed a number of specialized manuals, tailored to specific types of emergencies, such
as “Response to Fires in Electric and Hybrid Vehicles” (indsats ved brand i el- og hybridbiler),
which comprehensively covers the necessary knowledge for dealing with such incidents. The
cooperation with authorities has provided significant information and validation, effectively
bridging the gap between theoretical knowledge and practical application. While some Danish
manuals provide guidelines for the extinguishing of fires, the manual for electric and hybrid fires
offers both offensive and defensive tactics, as well as a combined approach for extinguishing
this type of vehicles. However, the “Response to Fires in Electric and Hybrid Vehicles” manual
offers specific guidance on the extinguishing process in a specific case than the FBIM manual,
which provides general, situationally-based information.
Although the tactics developed in this project are practical, more efficient methods for designing
these tactics may be needed. The process to be followed by firefighters is shown in Gantt
charts, highlighting that each firefighter is assigned a unique path that does not intersect with
others until the end of the operation, thereby promoting optimal cooperation. As a result of
this approach, a more detailed and realistic tactic is created, thereby increasing the precision
and effectiveness of the response as more accurate timing data are obtained.
mention of the comparison and standardization of the factors.

def tableA(time: int):
    green_color = '\033[92m'  # ANSI escape code for green text
    reset_color = '\033[0m'   # ANSI escape code to reset the color
    print()
    print(f"{green_color}Table A{reset_color}")
    print()
    print("Time to depressurise system and activate alarm")
    dataset = [
        {"System type": "AS 2118.1" , "Floor area of installation": "N/A", "Time": 360},
        {"System type": "Combined OHI", "Floor area of installation": "< 1 000 m2",
         "Time": 10},
        {"System type": "Combined OHI", 
         "Floor area of installation": "1 000 m2 < 2 000 m2", "Time": 20},
        {"System type": "Combined OHI", "Floor area of installation": "> 2 000 m2", "Time": 50}
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(dataset):
        print()
        print("Current Dataset:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(dataset):
            #drag and drop the line 25 with "-->" to print statement above (line 24)
            print(f"{i + 1}. System type: {entry['System type']}, Floor area of installation: {entry['Floor area of installation']} m2,-->
                  -->Time: {entry['Time']} sec")
    # Function to add a new car with custom criteria
    def add_system(dataset):
        print()
        system_type = input("Enter System type: ")
        floor_area = int(input("Enter Floor area of installation (m2): "))
        time = int(input("Enter Time (sec): "))
        new_data = {"System type": system_type, "Area": floor_area, "Time": time}
        dataset.append(new_data)
        # Stop the loop and return the time as an integer
        return time
    time = None  # Initialize time to None
    while time is None:
        display_dataset(dataset)
        print()
        print("\nOptions:")
        print("1. Choose a system from dataset")
        print("2. User input")
        print("3. Quit")
        print()
        choice = input("Choose the option: ")
        if choice == '1':
            index = int(input("Enter the index of the dataset you want to choose: "))
            if 1 <= index <= len(dataset):
                time = dataset[index - 1]["Time"]
                print()
                print(f"Selected Time (sec): {time}")
        elif choice == '2':
            time = add_system(dataset)
        elif choice == '3':
            break

        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid choice.")
    return int(time)

def tableB(time: int):
    # Define the dataset
    # Print name of the table B
    green_color = '\033[92m'  # ANSI escape code for green text
    reset_color = '\033[0m'   # ANSI escape code to reset the color
    print()
    print(f"{green_color}Table B{reset_color}")
    print()
    print("Times for alarms/fire verification and any notification delays")
    data = [
        ["Time delay for alarm verification", 20],
        ["Time to verify fire", None],
        ["Time delay until notification of fire brigade", None],
        ["Time delay for access, dial and connection", None],
        ["Time for special option to contact fire brigade", None]
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(data):
        print()
        print("Options:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(data):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {entry[0]}")
    selected_option = None  # Initialize selected_option to None
    time = None  # Initialize selected_time to None
    while selected_option is None or time is None:
        display_dataset(data)
        print()
        print("Choose a system from dataset")
        print("Quit")
        print()
        choice = input("Enter the index of the dataset you want to choose: ")
        if choice.lower() == 'quit':
            break
        elif choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(data):
            index = int(choice) - 1
            if data[index][1] is None:
                time = input(f"Enter time (sec) for option {index + 1}: ")
                data[index][1] = int(time)
                selected_option = data[index][0]
                time = int(time)
                print()
                print(f"Selected option: {selected_option}, Time set to {time} sec.")
            else:
                selected_option = data[index][0]
                time = data[index][1]
                print()
                print(f"Selected option: {selected_option}, Time: {time} sec.")
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid option number or 'quit' to quit.")

    return int(time)

def tableD(time: int):  # Set a default value for time
    dataset = [
         ["Special dispatch time to be assessed",None],
         ["Time to relay dispatch information by fully electronic CAD system",0],
3
==PAGE:182==
         ["Time to relay information by part manual CAD system",15],
         ["Time to relay dispatch information by phone or radio",30]
         ]
    while True:  # Use a loop to allow for re-tries on invalid input
            print("\nOptions:")
            print("1. Choose a system from dataset")
            print("2. Quit")
            print()
            choice = input("Enter your choice: ")
            if choice == '1':
                try:
                    index = int(input("Enter the index of the system you want to choose: "))
                    if 1 <= index <= len(dataset) and dataset[index - 1][1] is not None:
                        time = dataset[index - 1][1]  # Ensure time is always set to an integer value
                        print(f"Selected Time (sec): {time}")
                        break  # Exit the loop since a valid choice has been made
                    else:
                        print("Invalid index. Please enter a number within the dataset range.")
                except ValueError:
                    print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number.")
            elif choice == '2':
                break  # Exit the loop and return the current value of time
            else:
                print("Invalid choice. Please enter '1' to choose or '2' to quit.")
    return time

def tableY(time:int):
    # Initialize the dataset
    print("Table Y")
    print()
    print("Time for search and rescue")
    print()
    data = [
        ["Secondary search (m2/s/person)", 0.16],
        ["Remove/rescue person (m2/s/person)", 0.05],
        ["Primary search (m2/s/person)", 1.4]
    ]
    # Display the options
    print()
    print("Options:")
    for i, row in enumerate(data):
        print(f"{i + 1}. {row[0]}")
    while True:
        print()
        choice = input("Enter the number of the option you want to choose, 'q' to quit: ")
        if choice.lower() == 'q':
            print()
            print("Exiting the program.")
            return None
        elif choice.isdigit() and int(choice) <= len(data):
            index = int(choice) - 1
            time += data[index][1]
            return time
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid option number or 'q' to quit.")

def tableD(time: int):
    green_color = '\033[92m'  # ANSI escape code for green text
    reset_color = '\033[0m'   # ANSI escape code to reset the color
    print()
    print(f"{green_color}Table D{reset_color}")
    print()
    print("Times for dispatch")
    data = [
        ["Special dispatch time to be assessed",None],
        ["Time to relay dispatch information by fully electronic CAD system",int(0)],
        ["Time to relay information by part manual CAD system",int(15)],
        ["Time to relay dispatch information by phone or radio",int(30)]
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(data):
        print()
        print("Options:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(data):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {entry[0]}")
    selected_option = None  # Initialize selected_option to None
    time = None  # Initialize selected_time to None
    while selected_option is None or time is None:
        display_dataset(data)
        print()
        print("Choose a system from dataset")
        print("Quit")
        print()
        choice = input("Enter your choice: ")
        if choice.lower() == 'quit':
            break
        elif choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(data):
            index = int(choice) - 1
            if data[index][1] is None:
                time = input(f"Enter time (sec) for option {index + 1}: ")
                data[index][1] = int(time)
                selected_option = data[index][0]
                time = int(time)
                print()
                print(f"Selected option: {selected_option}, Time set to {time} sec.")
            else:
                selected_option = data[index][0]
                time = data[index][1]
                print()
                print(f"Selected option: {selected_option}, Time: {time} sec.")
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid option number or 'quit' to quit.")
    # Return the time as an integer
    return time

def table_F1(time: int):
    # Get user inputs
    print()
    print("Table F1")
    print()
    print("Time travel for brigade appliances")
    building_address = input("Enter Building Address: ")
    fire_station_address = input("Enter Appropriate/Agreed Fire Station Address: ")
    # Prompt user to insert distance manually
    print()
    print("Insert distance manually")
    # Get user input for distance in kilometers
    while True:
6
==PAGE:185==
        try:
            distance_km = float(input("Enter the distance in kilometers: "))
            if distance_km >= 0:
                # Speed of the fire brigade (45 km/h)
                speed_km_per_hour = 45
                # Calculate time in hours
                time_hours = distance_km / speed_km_per_hour
                # Convert time to seconds
                time = time_hours * 3600  # 1 hour = 3600 seconds
                print()
                print(f"Distance from {building_address} to {fire_station_address} is: {distance_km} km")
                print()
                print(f"The fire brigade takes {time:.2f} seconds to arrive at {building_address} address.")
                break
            else:
                print()
                print("Invalid input. Please enter a non-negative distance.")
        except ValueError:
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number.")
    return int(time)

def table_F2(time:int):
    # Initialize the dataset
    print()
    print("Table F2")
    print()
    print("Time travel for brigade appliance")
    data = [["Appliance speed for travel through site", 8]]
    # Print the activity and speed
    print()
    print("Options:")
    for i, row in enumerate(data):
        print(f"{i + 1}: {row[0]} (Speed: {row[1]} km/hour)")
    # Ask the user to choose the option
    while True:
        try:
            choice = int(input("Choose an option (1): "))
            if choice == 1:
                selected_option = data[choice - 1]
                speed = selected_option[1]
                break
            else:
                print()
                print("Invalid choice. Please choose option 1.")
        except ValueError:
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number.")
    # Ask the user to enter the distance in kilometers
    while True:
        try:
            distance_km = float(input("Enter the distance in kilometers: "))
            if distance_km >= 0:
                # Calculate time in hours
                time_hours = distance_km / speed
                # Convert time to minutes
                time_minutes = time_hours * 60 * 60
7
==PAGE:186==
                # Convert time to integer (rounding down)
                time = int(time_minutes)
                print()
                print(f"Time required: {time} sec")
                break
            else:
                print()
                print("Invalid input. Please enter a non-negative distance.")
        except ValueError:
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number.")
    return int(time)

def tableG(time: int):
    # Define the dataset
    # Print name of the table G
    print()
    print("Table G")
    print()
    print("Time delay for building entry")
    data = [
        ["Time for any security procedure", None]
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(data):
        print()
        print("Options:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(data):
            print(f"{i + 1}. {entry[0]}")
    selected_option = None  # Initialize selected_option to None
    time = None  # Initialize selected_time to None
    while selected_option is None or time is None:
        display_dataset(data)
        print()
        print("Choose a security procedure from the dataset")
        print()
        print("Quit")
        choice = input("Enter your choice: ")
        if choice.lower() == 'Quit':
            break
        elif choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(data):
            index = int(choice) - 1
            selected_option = data[index][0]
            time = input("Enter time (sec) for the selected security procedure: ")

            data[index][1] = time
            print()
            print(f"Selected security procedure: {selected_option}, Time set to {time} sec.")
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid option number or 'quit' to quit.")
    # Return the selected security procedure and time as an integer
    return int(time)

8
==PAGE:187==
    # Print name of the table H
    print("Table H")
    print()
    print("Time to communicate with warden")
    print()
    dataset = [
        {"Building floor area m2": "< 1000", "Time": 30},
        {"Building floor area m2": "1000 - 5000", "Time": 45},
        {"Building floor area m2": "> 5000", "Time": 90}
    ]
    floor_area = int(input("Enter the building floor area (m2): "))
    time = None
    for entry in dataset:
        if entry["Building floor area m2"] == "< 1000" and floor_area < 1000:
            time = entry["Time"]
            break
        elif entry["Building floor area m2"] == "1000 - 5000" and 1000 <= floor_area <= 5000:
            time = entry["Time"]
            break
        elif entry["Building floor area m2"] == "> 5000" and floor_area > 5000:
            time = entry["Time"]
            break
    if time is not None:
        print()
        print(f"Selected Time (sec): {time}")
        return int(time)
    else:
        print()
        print("No matching row found for the entered floor area.")
        return None

def tableK(time: int):
    # Initialize the dataset
    # Print name of the table 
    print()
    print("Table K")
    print()
    print("Time to resolve way finding")
    dataset = [
        {"Complexity/building size": "Multi-level numerious enclosures & passages", "Time": 30},
        {"Complexity/building size": "Multi-level, open plan", "Time": 10},
        {"Complexity/building size": "Single storey, numerous enclosures & passages, floor area > 5000 m2","Time": 45},
        {"Complexity/building size": "Single storey, open plan", "Time": 10},
        {"Complexity/building size": "Single storey, numerous enclosures & passages, floor area < 5000 m2", "Time": 30}
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(dataset):
        print()
        print("Current Dataset:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(dataset):
            print(f"{i + 1}. Complexity/building size: {entry['Complexity/building size']}, Time: {entry['Time']} sec")
    # Function to add a new car with custom criteria
    def add_system(dataset):
        complexity_building_size = input("Complexity/building size: ")
        time = int(input("Enter Time (sec): "))
        new_data = {"Complexity/building size": complexity_building_size, "Time": time}
        dataset.append(new_data)
        # Stop the loop and return the time as an integer
        return time
    time = None  # Initialize time to None
    while time is None:
        display_dataset(dataset)
        print()
        print("\nOptions:")
        print("1. Choose a Complexity/building size from dataset")
        print("2. User input")
        print("3. Quit")
        print()
        choice = input("Enter your choice: ")
        if choice == '1':
            index = int(input("Enter the index of the Complexity/Building size you want to choose: "))
            if 1 <= index <= len(dataset):
                time = dataset[index - 1]["Time"]
                print()
                print(f"Selected Time (sec): {time}")
        elif choice == '2':
            time = add_system(dataset)
        elif choice == '3':
            break
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid choice.")
    return int(time)

def tableR(time: int):
    # Initialize the dataset
    # Print the name of the table R
    print("Table R")
    print()
    print("Firefighter Vertical Travel Speed")
    print()
    dataset = [
        ["Fireman’s lift", None],
        ["Loading time", 30]
    ]
    # Display the initial dataset
    def display_dataset(dataset):
        print()
        print("Options:")
        for i, entry in enumerate(dataset):
            print(f"{i + 1}. Conditions: {entry[0]}, Speed (m/sec): {entry[1]}")
    display_dataset(dataset)
    while True:
        choice = input("Enter the number of the option you want to choose, or 'q' to quit: ")
        if choice.lower() == 'q':
            break
        elif choice.isdigit() and 1 <= int(choice) <= len(dataset):
            index = int(choice) - 1
            selected_speed = dataset[index][1]
            if selected_speed is None:
                print()
                selected_speed = float(input("Enter the firefighter's vertical travel speed (m/sec): "))
                dataset[index][1] = selected_speed
            distance = float(input("Enter the distance (meters): "))
            time = distance / selected_speed 
            print()
            print(f"Time for Vertical Travel (sec): {time}")
            return int(time)
        else:
            print()
            print("Invalid choice. Please enter a valid option number or 'q' to quit.")

    while True:
        try:
            print()
            T_water = float(input("Enter the temperature of the water (default temp 10 deg C): ") or 10)
            break
        except ValueError:
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number for the temperature of the water.")
    # Calculate E_water
    E_water = (100 - T_water) * 0.00418
    print()
    print(f"E_water = {E_water} MJ/kg")
    
    # Calculate E_steam
    E_steam = 2.26  # Constant value for E_steam
    print()
    print(f"E_steam = {E_steam} MJ/kg")
    # Input for T_room
    while True:
        try:
            T_room = float(input("Enter the temperature of the room (temperature pre/post flashover): "))
            break
        except ValueError:
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number for the temperature of the room.")
    # Calculate E_room
    E_room = (T_room - 100) * 0.00201
    print()
    print(f"E_room = {E_room} MJ/kg")
    # Calculate E_total
    E_total = E_water + E_steam + E_room
    print()
    print(f"Total cooling capacity: {E_total} MW pr L/s")
    return int(E_total)

def ask_travel_time():
    time_delay.sleep(1)
    print()
    while True:
        time = input("Q2: Travel time (sec): ")
        try:
            time = int(time)
            if time >= 0:
                return time
            else:
                time_delay.sleep(1)
                print()
                print("Invalid input. Travel time must be >= 0.")
        except ValueError:
            time_delay.sleep(1)
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter a valid number for travel time (sec).")
def ask_another_appliance():
    time_delay.sleep(1)
    print()
    while True:
        response = input("Q3: Is another appliance responding from another location? (Yes/No): ").strip().lower()
        if response == "yes":
            return True
        elif response == "no":
            return False
        else:
            time_delay.sleep(1)
            print()
            print("Invalid input. Please enter 'Yes' or 'No'.")

    if answer2.lower() == "yes":

        time += time_table_1
        time_delay.sleep(1)

        print(f"A3: Time for any security procedures ({time_table_1} sec.)")
        time_table_2 = tui35.user_input_34(time)
        time += time_table_2
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        print(f"A4: Time to travel through the site = travel distance divided by travel ({time_table_2} sec.)")
        time = question5(time)
    elif answer2.lower() == "no":
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        time = question5(time)
    else:
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        print("Invalid input. Please enter 'Yes' or 'No'.")
        time = question2(time)
    return time

def question2(time):
    global num_teams  # Declare num_teams as global
    answer2 = input("Q2: Have firefighter safety limits been exceeded in the enclosure? (Yes/No): ")
    if answer2.lower() == "yes":
        print("D3: Search cannot be undertaken in that enclosure, possible loss of life or property. Proceed to chart 13.")
    elif answer2.lower() == "no":
        print("How many search teams are available with a charged line of hose? ")
        num_teams = int(input("Number of teams: "))
        time = question5(time)
    else:
        print("Invalid input. Please enter 'Yes' or 'No'.")
        time = question2(time)
    return time

def step_1(time: int):
    print("\nImporting Chart 11")
    time_chart_11 = c11.chart11(time)
    time += time_chart_11
    time_delay.sleep(1)

def calculate_q_max():
    q_max = float(input("Enter the Q_max in MW: "))
    time_delay.sleep(1)
    print()
    return q_max
def select_volume_attack():
    while True:
        attack_type = input("Select the type of attack (HP, B, C): ").upper()
        if attack_type in ["HP", "B", "C"]:
            num_hoses = int(input("Enter the number of hoses used: "))
            volume = {"HP": 10, "B": 20 / 3, "C": 10 / 3}.get(attack_type) * num_hoses
            time_delay.sleep(1)
            print()
            return volume
        else:
            print("Invalid attack type!")
def calculate_extinguishing_capacity(volume):
    w_cool = 5 / 8  # [L/s]/[MW]
    q_ex = volume / w_cool
    time_delay.sleep(1)
    print()
    return q_ex
def check_water_effect(time, q_ex, q_max):
    if q_ex >= 1.2 * q_max:
        print("Decay of the fire")
        time_delay.sleep(1)
49
==PAGE:254==
        print()
    elif q_ex >= 1.1 * q_max:
        print("Control of the fire")
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
    elif q_ex < 0.9 * q_max:
        print("No effect on the fire")
    return time
def question5(time, q_ex):
    answer5 = input("Q5: Is the heat release rate reducing over time? (Yes/No): ")
    if answer5.lower() == "yes":
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        hrr_tot = float(input("Enter the total amount of energy the object got in MW: "))
        time_decay = int(hrr_tot / q_ex)
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        print(f"Time to extinguish the fire: {time_decay} sec")
        time += time_decay
    elif answer5.lower() == "no":
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        time = question7(time)
    else:
        time_delay.sleep(1)
        print()
        print("Invalid input. Please enter 'Yes' or 'No'.")
        time = question5(time)
    return time
